   - Increase inner title block from `space-y-4` to `space-y-5`.
   - Increase top padding before buttons from `pt-2` to `pt-4` for clearer separation. (All using existing Tailwind scale; no new containers.)

4. **Responsiveness**
   - Removing the forced `<br />` lets the subtitle reflow cleanly on small screens.

5. **Visual Hierarchy**
   - h1 stays `text-foreground` (primary), positioning statement stays `text-muted-foreground` (secondary), description stays `text-muted-foreground/80` (tertiary). No new colors or accent treatments introduced, preserving the monochrome/dark-only language from `STYLE_GUIDE.md`.

Current homepage structure (from the file):
- Hero section: Logo, H1 "Public Intelligence", subtitle "Building a globally distributed, community-owned AI infrastructure." with br, description paragraph, two buttons (Explore Architecture, GitHub).
- Section 01: System Diagram (Distributed Inference Coordination) with description and SystemDiagram component.
- Section 02: Foundational Principles (4 items with small SVGs).
- Section 03: Active Roadmap (Phase 1).
- Footer: Logo, links, copyright, version.

Now, act as senior product designer.

1. Three biggest weaknesses:
- (a) Weak information hierarchy / scanning rhythm in hero: The hero crams a logo, title, a broken-line subtitle, a paragraph, and buttons without a clear focal anchor. The subtitle uses a `<br>` which is a brittle typographic hack; on different viewports it creates awkward ragging. The description paragraph is similar in weight to the subtitle (both muted-foreground), reducing the "immediate communication" of the core mission.
- (b) Decorative/ambiguous iconography in principles: The custom inline SVGs for the 4 principles are low-fidelity, visually inconsistent (different stroke opacities, some filled, some not), and don't clearly map to the text. They add noise rather than clarity, conflicting with the "icons only if they communicate necessary UI function" rule in the style guide.
- (c) The "memorable visual moment" (System Diagram) sits too high / lacks context: The hero is followed immediately by a schematic with a dense technical label ("01 // ARCHITECTURAL TOPOLOGY") before the reader has understood the *why*. The diagram is an SVG with monochrome lines and one highlighted path, but it's presented as a equal-weight section rather than a supported visual aid. The homepage feels like a spec dump rather than a guided narrative.

2. Three strongest aspects:
- (a) Restraint and consistency: The monochrome palette, limited type scale, and consistent use of small mono uppercase labels (`01 // ARCHITECTURAL TOPOLOGY`) create a coherent, serious engineering aesthetic that matches the stated goals.
- (b) Clear, documentation-first copy: The writing is calm, direct, and avoids hype. The principles and milestone text are precise and give a trustworthy impression.
- (c) Structural semantics: Uses semantic HTML (`section`, `header`, `nav`, `footer`, `aria-labelledby`), and the `PageShell` wrapper keeps content constrained. This is a solid foundation for accessibility and maintainability.

3. What prevents it from feeling world-class:
- Lack of a clear "hero statement" that commands attention. World-class engineering sites (e.g., Rust, Deno, Fly.io) use a sharp, large, well-spaced value proposition with a single dominant visual or typographic moment. Here, the hero is visually quiet to the point of being inert; the accent color `#D9F99D` is used for tiny labels but not to draw the eye to the most important claim.
- The custom SVG diagrams (system diagram, principle icons) look amateurish compared to the typographic polish expected. World-class sites either use extremely refined custom graphics or rely purely on type and whitespace.
- No responsive typographic refinement: sizes jump but don't adapt line-lengths or spacing gracefully; the `<br>` in the hero is a tell-tale sign of unrefined responsive type.
- The footer and section dividers are fine but the overall page reads as a template, not a crafted narrative.

4. Highest impact changes preserving design language:
- (a) Rebuild the hero as a typographic manifesto: Remove the `<br>`, enlarge the core mission statement to be the primary visual element (using `text-balance` and tighter leading), and use the `#D9F99D` accent *once* on a key word or the small label to create a focal point. This keeps monochrome + one accent, improves hierarchy, and immediately communicates the distributed AI mission.
- (b) Replace the four custom principle icons with a strict typographic list (numbered or labeled) or extremely minimal, consistent geometric marks. This aligns with "icons only if necessary" and reduces visual noise.
- (c) Re-architect the section flow: Move the "Foundational Principles" before the System Diagram, or integrate the diagram into the architecture section link more subtly, so the homepage tells a story: Mission -> Principles -> How it works -> Status. This improves comprehension without adding sections.

**Design Critique: Public Intelligence Homepage (Senior Product Designer Lens)**

*Context: Analysis based on the provided `src/app/page.tsx` and the constraints in `docs/STYLE_GUIDE.md`, `docs/WEBSITE_SPEC.md`, and `docs/DEVELOPMENT.md`. The stated design language is “minimal, dark-only, typography-first, monochrome, quiet, precise, durable.”*

---

### 1. The Three Biggest Weaknesses

**a) Brittle Typographic Hierarchy in the Hero**
The hero stacks a logo, an `<h1>`, a subtitle with a hard-coded `<br>`, a description paragraph, and two buttons—all within uniform `space-y` gaps. The subtitle (“Building a globally distributed, community-owned AI infrastructure.”) is broken by a `<br>` that assumes a specific viewport width; on smaller or larger screens it rags awkwardly. More importantly, the subtitle and the description paragraph are both rendered in `text-muted-foreground` (or `/80`), making them nearly identical in visual weight. The reader’s eye is not pulled to the single most important claim (the distributed AI mission) because nothing in the type scale or color creates a clear primary/secondary/tertiary rhythm beyond size alone.

**b) Low-Fidelity, Inconsistent Iconography**
The “Foundational Principles” section uses four hand-rolled inline SVGs (community, open source, docs, simplicity). They use mixed stroke opacities, inconsistent geometry, and lack a unified visual logic. They read as decorative placeholders rather than intentional marks. This directly conflicts with the style guide’s rule: “Icons unless they communicate necessary UI function.” Here they communicate nothing the heading doesn’t already say, and they add visual noise that undermines the “precise, quiet” goal.

**c) Inert “Visual Moment” Placement**
The System Diagram is presented immediately after the hero under the label “01 // ARCHITECTURAL TOPOLOGY.” A reader lands on a documentation-style schematic before they have absorbed the *why* behind the project. The diagram itself is a functional SVG, but as the first thing below the fold it acts as a density wall rather than a guided reveal. The homepage reads as a spec dump, not a narrative.

---

### 2. The Three Strongest Aspects

**a) Disciplined Visual Restraint**
The monochrome palette, the single restrained accent (`#D9F99D`) used only for small mono labels, and the consistent Tailwind utility spacing create a coherent, serious engineering aesthetic. It successfully avoids the “startup landing page” trap called out in the spec.

**b) Calm, Documentation-First Copy**
The writing is direct, non-hype, and technically literate. The principle descriptions and the roadmap milestone are precise and trustworthy. This matches the intended audience (engineers, researchers, contributors) extremely well.

**c) Sound Semantic Foundation**
The markup uses `section`, `aria-labelledby`, `nav`, and `footer` correctly. The `PageShell` wrapper and max-width constraints are textbook documentation layout. This gives the site a durable, accessible base that is rare in early-stage project sites.

---

### 3. What Prevents It from Feeling World-Class

- **No Typographic Focal Point:** World-class engineering sites (e.g., Rust, Deno, Fly.io) use one dominant typographic moment—a large, well-leaded statement that commands attention. Here, the hero is visually quiet to the point of being passive. The accent color is wasted on tiny labels instead of drawing the eye to the core mission.
- **Amateur Graphic Execution:** The custom SVG diagrams and principle icons look unrefined next to the typographic intent. World-class sites either invest in pixel-perfect custom graphics or go pure-type. The current middle-ground reads as “template.”
- **Lack of Responsive Type Refinement:** The `<br>` in the hero and the uniform scaling (`sm:text-5xl`, `md:text-6xl`) without adjusting line-length or spacing per breakpoint shows the type system is inherited, not crafted.
- **Narrative Flatness:** The page is a sequence of equal-weight blocks. There is no rise and fall in information density, so it feels like a README rendered as a webpage rather than a considered product surface.

---

### 4. Highest-Impact Changes (Preserving Design Language)

*(Conceptual only—no implementation yet)*

**a) Elevate the Hero to a Typographic Manifesto**
Remove the `<br>`, let the mission statement become the visual anchor (using `text-balance`, tighter leading, and a slight size bump), and use the existing `#D9F99D` accent *once*—either on a key phrase or a small kicker label—to create a focal point. This keeps the monochrome+single-accent language but fixes the hierarchy and immediately communicates the distributed-AI mission.

**b) Demote or Unify the Principle Icons**
Strip the four custom SVGs and replace them with a strict typographic treatment (e.g., numbered mono labels `01–04` matching the existing section style). This aligns with the “icons only if necessary” rule, reduces noise, and makes the section feel intentional rather than decorated.

**c) Re-Sequence the Narrative Flow**
Swap the order so the reader gets Mission → Principles → System Diagram → Roadmap. This turns the diagram into a payoff after the principles are understood, improving comprehension without adding sections, dependencies, or new design elements.

---

*This is a critique only. No code or file listings are provided per your instruction. After you review, tell me which single improvement you’d like to implement, and I will plan and (upon approval) edit only the necessary file.*

---

# Brand Guidelines

## Purpose
Design at Public Intelligence is not a layer of persuasion placed on top of engineering. It is the public face of a long-term civic undertaking. Its role is to make serious technical work legible, trustworthy, and calm. Good design here reduces noise, reveals structure, and helps readers evaluate substance without distraction. The website, documentation, and every public artifact should feel like part of a permanent public utility—built to be used, audited, and extended for decades.

## Emotional Goals
Public Intelligence should greet readers with quiet ambition: the sense that they have encountered the early foundations of a durable public institution, not a startup seeking attention.

- Within 5 seconds: The reader should feel they have stepped onto serious ground. The absence of color, motion, or sales language creates immediate respect. Seeing the project's name beside its core mission produces a subtle jolt—this is a proposition about shared technological power, not a product. The dominant feeling is calm gravity.
- After 30 seconds: The reader should feel intellectual trust. The copy is precise and hype-free. They understand the project is decentralized, open, and documentation-driven. If they are a builder, they feel alignment. The monochrome calm reads as confidence. They sense disciplined minds behind the words.
- After reading the entire website: The reader should feel they have been handed a blueprint for a decades-long public asset. They feel sober optimism—realism about difficulty paired with clarity of intent. No false urgency. They leave with steadiness: this is built to outlast trends, and they know where to look next.

Quiet ambition means we aim for civilization-scale impact while speaking in a measured, restrained voice.

## Brand Personality
Public Intelligence is:
- Thoughtful
- Precise
- Engineering-first
- Calm
- Durable
- Transparent
- Ambitious without being loud

Public Intelligence is NOT:
- Hype
- Crypto-speculative
- Futuristic gimmickry
- Startup marketing
- Artificial urgency
- AI buzzword-driven

The personality is that of a public works engineer who writes clear specs, not a founder who pitches.

## Writing Style
Every page should be written as documentation for a serious technical audience.
- Sentence length: Prefer short, direct sentences. Break complex thoughts into separate lines.
- Tone: Calm, neutral, active where practical. No exclamation. No persuasion.
- Technical depth: Assume the reader is technically literate. Do not flatten nuance.
- Jargon: Use precise technical terms when they carry meaning. Do not use vague business or AI-industry slang.
- Marketing language: Prohibited. No testimonials, no "seamless", no "revolutionary", no urgency cues.

## Visual Principles
- Typography: The primary design material. Clear, restrained, readable. Hierarchy from size and spacing, not decoration.
- Whitespace: Generous. Used to create scanability and rhythm. Not to simulate importance.
- Color philosophy: Dark-only, monochrome. One restrained accent for necessary emphasis. No gradients, no new brand colors.
- Iconography: Only when it communicates necessary UI function. No decorative icons.
- Diagrams: Allowed when they explain structure. They should be precise, monochrome, and quiet.
- Illustrations: None. The work is serious; imagery distracts.
- Animation: None unless it clarifies function. No motion for persuasion.
- Imagery: None. The project is explained through text and structure.

## Homepage Philosophy
The homepage is an entry point, not a campaign. Its narrative journey is deliberate:

Mission → Architecture → Progress → Contribution

The reader first meets the core intent (what we are building and why). They then see the technical shape of the system (how it is structured). Next they view current progress and roadmap (what is real today). Finally they are shown how to take part (contribution).

This order exists because understanding must precede action. A reader who knows the mission can judge the architecture. A reader who sees the architecture can trust the progress. A reader who trusts the progress will contribute meaningfully. The homepage is a guided intellectual path, not a funnel.

## Public Intelligence as an Institution
Public Intelligence is building public digital infrastructure, not a startup or a product.

If the project exists for 30 years, its name should be associated with:
- Reliable, community-owned technical commons
- Transparent engineering practiced at scale
- A stable reference point for open AI infrastructure

Every repository—whether website, documentation, scheduler, node software, research paper, or presentation—should feel like a component of the same public institution. It should feel considered, permanent, and auditable. The feeling should resemble enduring scientific and archival organizations that exist to serve the public over generations, not entities optimized for exit or growth metrics.

The values every repository communicates:
- Stewardship of shared resources
- Openness by default
- Resistance to fashion
- Long-term maintainability

Over time, contributors and users should develop a specific trust: that Public Intelligence will still be operating on the same principles in a decade, that its artifacts will be comprehensible, and that no hidden commercial shift will redirect the mission. This trust is earned through consistency, not claims.

## Long-term Consistency
Future contributors and AI agents should evaluate every design change against this constitution:

1. Does it increase calm and clarity, or add noise?
2. Does it preserve the monochrome, typography-first language?
3. Does it communicate substance before persuasion?
4. Would this change still make sense in ten years?
5. Does it respect the reader's intelligence?

If a proposed change fails these tests, it does not belong in Public Intelligence, regardless of trend. The brand is a commitment across time.

# Brand Guidelines

## Purpose

Design at Public Intelligence is not a layer of persuasion placed on top of engineering. It is the public face of a long-term civic undertaking. Its role is to make serious technical work legible, trustworthy, and calm. Good design here reduces noise, reveals structure, and helps readers evaluate substance without distraction. The website, documentation, and every public artifact should feel like part of a permanent public utility—built to be used, audited, and extended for decades.

## Emotional Goals

Public Intelligence should greet readers with quiet ambition: the sense that they have encountered the early foundations of a durable public institution, not a startup seeking attention.

- **Within 5 seconds:** The reader should feel they have stepped onto serious ground. The absence of color, motion, or sales language creates immediate respect. Seeing the project's name beside its core mission produces a subtle jolt—this is a proposition about shared technological power, not a product. The dominant feeling is calm gravity.
- **After 30 seconds:** The reader should feel intellectual trust. The copy is precise and hype-free. They understand the project is decentralized, open, and documentation-driven. If they are a builder, they feel alignment. The monochrome calm reads as confidence. They sense disciplined minds behind the words.
- **After reading the entire website:** The reader should feel they have been handed a blueprint for a decades-long public asset. They feel sober optimism—realism about difficulty paired with clarity of intent. No false urgency. They leave with steadiness: this is built to outlast trends, and they know where to look next.

Quiet ambition means we aim for civilization-scale impact while speaking in a measured, restrained voice.

## Brand Personality

Public Intelligence is:

- Thoughtful
- Precise
- Engineering-first
- Calm
- Durable
- Transparent
- Ambitious without being loud

Public Intelligence is NOT:

- Hype
- Crypto-speculative
- Futuristic gimmickry
- Startup marketing
- Artificial urgency
- AI buzzword-driven

The personality is that of a public works engineer who writes clear specs, not a founder who pitches.

## Writing Style

Every page should be written as documentation for a serious technical audience.

- **Sentence length:** Prefer short, direct sentences. Break complex thoughts into separate lines.
- **Tone:** Calm, neutral, active where practical. No exclamation. No persuasion.
- **Technical depth:** Assume the reader is technically literate. Do not flatten nuance.
- **Jargon:** Use precise technical terms when they carry meaning. Do not use vague business or AI-industry slang.
- **Marketing language:** Prohibited. No testimonials, no "seamless", no "revolutionary", no urgency cues.

## Visual Principles

- **Typography:** The primary design material. Clear, restrained, readable. Hierarchy from size and spacing, not decoration.
- **Whitespace:** Generous. Used to create scanability and rhythm. Not to simulate importance.
- **Color philosophy:** Dark-only, monochrome. One restrained accent for necessary emphasis. No gradients, no new brand colors.
- **Iconography:** Only when it communicates necessary UI function. No decorative icons.
- **Diagrams:** Allowed when they explain structure. They should be precise, monochrome, and quiet.
- **Illustrations:** None. The work is serious; imagery distracts.
- **Animation:** None unless it clarifies function. No motion for persuasion.
- **Imagery:** None. The project is explained through text and structure.

## Homepage Philosophy

The homepage is an entry point, not a campaign. Its narrative journey is deliberate:

Mission → Architecture → Progress → Contribution

The reader first meets the core intent (what we are building and why). They then see the technical shape of the system (how it is structured). Next they view current progress and roadmap (what is real today). Finally they are shown how to take part (contribution).

This order exists because understanding must precede action. A reader who knows the mission can judge the architecture. A reader who sees the architecture can trust the progress. A reader who trusts the progress will contribute meaningfully. The homepage is a guided intellectual path, not a funnel.

## Public Intelligence as an Institution

Public Intelligence is building public digital infrastructure, not a startup or a product.

If the project exists for 30 years, its name should be associated with:

- Reliable, community-owned technical commons
- Transparent engineering practiced at scale
- A stable reference point for open AI infrastructure

Every repository—whether website, documentation, scheduler, node software, research paper, or presentation—should feel like a component of the same public institution. It should feel considered, permanent, and auditable. The feeling should resemble enduring scientific and archival organizations that exist to serve the public over generations, not entities optimized for exit or growth metrics.

The values every repository communicates:

- Stewardship of shared resources
- Openness by default
- Resistance to fashion
- Long-term maintainability

Over time, contributors and users should develop a specific trust: that Public Intelligence will still be operating on the same principles in a decade, that its artifacts will be comprehensible, and that no hidden commercial shift will redirect the mission. This trust is earned through consistency, not claims.

## Long-term Consistency

Future contributors and AI agents should evaluate every design change against this constitution:

1. Does it increase calm and clarity, or add noise?
2. Does it preserve the monochrome, typography-first language?
3. Does it communicate substance before persuasion?
4. Would this change still make sense in ten years?
5. Does it respect the reader's intelligence?

If a proposed change fails these tests, it does not belong in Public Intelligence, regardless of trend. The brand is a commitment across time.

## Senior Product Designer Review: Cross-Page Consistency Audit

*Note: This review is based on the full `src/app/page.tsx` (homepage) and the truncated summaries of `architecture`, `contribute`, `roadmap`, `vision`, and `research` pages provided earlier, plus the shared components and docs. For exact implementation, the full inner-page files would be added to chat.*

---

### 1. Inconsistencies Identified

**A. Section Kicker / Accent Color Drift**
- Homepage and `architecture`/`vision` pages use `text-[#D9F99D]` for the small mono uppercase label (e.g., `01 // ARCHITECTURAL TOPOLOGY`).
- `contribute` and `roadmap` pages use `text-muted-foreground/60` for the same role.
- This makes the site feel like it has two different "brands" depending on which page you land on.

**B. Header Composition**
- Homepage hero includes a `Logo`, an `<h1>`, a forced-break subtitle, a description, and two CTA buttons.
- Inner pages use a `<header>` with a mono kicker, an `<h1>`, and (presumably) a description, but no logo, no buttons, and no consistent subtitle treatment.
- The homepage is the only page with a numbered section system (`01 //`, `02 //`, `03 //`); inner pages lack this structural rhythm, making them feel less "engineered."

**C. Footer Presence**
- Only the homepage contains a footer (copyright, version, nav links).
- Inner pages end at the last `<section>` inside `PageShell` with no footer, leaving the reader at a dead stop. This is the clearest sign of "unfinished" pages.

**D. Diagram Ownership**
- Homepage uses `SystemDiagram` (viewBox `760x180`).
- Architecture page uses `ArchitectureDiagram`, `DistributedInferenceDiagram`, `PlatformStackDiagram` (viewBox `760x280/240`).
- Each diagram component is hand-built with its own `defs` and stroke opacities. Without a shared diagram primitive, visual consistency is accidental.

---

### 2. Weak Diagrams

- **Homepage Principle Icons (in `page.tsx`):** Four inline SVGs with mixed stroke opacities (`strokeOpacity="0.3"`, `0.4`, `0.5`) and inconsistent geometry. They violate the new `BRAND_GUIDELINES.md` ("Iconography: Only when it communicates necessary UI function. No decorative icons") and look amateurish next to the precise diagrams.
- **SystemDiagram:** Acceptable as a quiet schematic, but its styling is isolated from the architecture diagrams; no shared stroke-width or color token is used.

---

### 3. Weak Typography

- **Homepage Subtitle:** Uses a hard `<br />` ("Building a globally distributed,<br />community-owned AI infrastructure.") that breaks at arbitrary widths and contradicts the responsive principles in `STYLE_GUIDE.md`.
- **Inner Page H1:** Snippets show `text-4xl ... sm:text-5xl sm:lea...` (likely `sm:leading-tight`), while homepage uses `sm:leading-[1.1]`. Inconsistent leading between pages.
- **Body Copy:** Homepage description is `text-base leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground/80`; inner pages likely use similar but the exact class set isn't standardized.

---

### 4. Weak Hierarchy

- Homepage creates clear primary (h1) → secondary (subtitle) → tertiary (description) via size and color, but the subtitle and description are both muted, weakening the "distributed AI" message.
- Inner pages have no subtitle, so the h1 sits directly on the description—less narrative pull.
- The homepage's `01/02/03` labeled sections establish a strong documentation cadence; inner pages have no equivalent labeling, so their content reads as a flat blob.

---

### 5. Pages That Feel Unfinished

- **`/research`**: No content summary provided; likely a stub.
- **All inner pages**: Missing footer, missing section numbering, missing consistent kicker color.
- **`/contribute` & `/roadmap`**: Wrong kicker color (muted instead of accent), making them feel like lower-priority drafts.

---

### Prioritized Implementation Plan (No Redesign, Just Cohesion)

**P0 — Establish a Shared Page Header & Footer (eliminates "unfinished" feel)**
- Create a `PageHeader` component (or standardize markup) that all pages use: mono kicker in `#D9F99D`, `h1` with `sm:leading-[1.1]`, optional description. This fixes accent drift and header composition.
- Extract the homepage footer into a `SiteFooter` component and include it in `PageShell` (or at end of each page) so every page gets the copyright/nav closure.

**P1 — Unify Accent & Typography Tokens**
- Update `contribute` and `roadmap` kickers to use `text-[#D9F99D]` (or a CSS variable) to match architecture/vision/home.
- Standardize `h1` leading and subtitle treatment across all pages. Remove the `<br />` from homepage subtitle.

**P2 — Remove Decorative Icons, Align with Brand Constitution**
- Replace the four homepage principle SVGs with typographic numbered labels (`01–04`) matching the existing section style, satisfying `BRAND_GUIDELINES.md` and `STYLE_GUIDE.md`.

**P3 — Diagram Consistency Pass**
- Audit `SystemDiagram` and architecture diagrams to ensure identical stroke widths, font-mono usage, and muted/stroke opacities. (No new component required, just align the existing SVG attributes.)

**P4 — Section Numbering on Inner Pages**
- Add the `0X //` mono label pattern to inner page sections where natural (e.g., Vision, Architecture, Roadmap) so the entire site shares the same "engineered documentation" rhythm.

**Files likely to be modified (after approval & full file add):**
- `src/components/page-header.tsx` (new, or edit existing)
- `src/components/site-footer.tsx` (new, or extract)
- `src/components/page-shell.tsx` (to include footer)
- `src/app/page.tsx` (remove `<br>`, remove icons, use new header/footer)
- `src/app/architecture/page.tsx`, `src/app/vision/page.tsx`, `src/app/roadmap/page.tsx`, `src/app/contribute/page.tsx`, `src/app/research/page.tsx` (adopt shared header, fix kicker color, add footer via shell)

---

**site-footer.tsx**
```tsx
import Link from "next/link";

const links = [
  { href: "/vision", label: "Vision" },
  { href: "/architecture", label: "Architecture" },
  { href: "/research", label: "Research" },
  { href: "/roadmap", label: "Roadmap" },
  {
    href: "https://github.com/Public-Intelligence-Revolution",
    label: "GitHub",
    external: true,
  },
];

export function SiteFooter() {
  return (
    <footer className="space-y-8 pt-16 border-t border-border/20 text-xs text-muted-foreground/60">
      <div className="flex flex-wrap items-center justify-between gap-6">
        <div className="inline-flex items-center gap-2">
          <span className="w-4 h-4 text-muted-foreground/50">PI</span>
          <span>Public Intelligence — Open Infrastructure Initiative</span>
        </div>
        <nav aria-label="Footer navigation" className="flex flex-wrap gap-x-6 gap-y-2">
          {links.map((link) => (
            <Link
              key={link.href}
              href={link.href}
              className="hover:text-[#D9F99D] transition-colors duration-150"
              target={link.external ? "_blank" : undefined}
              rel={link.external ? "noreferrer" : undefined}
            >
              {link.label}
            </Link>
          ))}
        </nav>
      </div>
      <div className="flex items-center justify-between text-[10px] border-t border-border/10 pt-6 font-mono opacity-80">
        <p>© {new Date().getFullYear()} Public Intelligence. Released under the MIT License.</p>
        <p>VER_0.1.0 // FOUNDATIONAL_RELEASE</p>
      </div>
    </footer>
  );
}
```
Wait, original footer used `<Logo className="w-4 h-4 ..." />`. I'll import Logo to keep consistency.

**page-header.tsx**
```tsx
import * as React from "react";

type PageHeaderProps = {
  kicker: string;
  title: string;
  description?: string;
};

export function PageHeader({ kicker, title, description }: PageHeaderProps) {
  return (
    <header className="space-y-6">
      <span className="text-xs font-mono uppercase tracking-wider text-[#D9F99D]">{kicker}</span>
      <div className="space-y-4">
        <h1 className="text-4xl font-semibold tracking-tight text-foreground sm:text-5xl sm:leading-[1.15]">
          {title}
        </h1>
        {description && (
          <p className="max-w-3xl text-xl leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-2xl font-light">
            {description}
          </p>
        )}
      </div>
    </header>
  );
}
```

src/components/site-footer.tsx
````
import Link from "next/link";
import { Logo } from "@/components/logo";

const links = [
  { href: "/vision", label: "Vision" },
  { href: "/architecture", label: "Architecture" },
  { href: "/research", label: "Research" },
  { href: "/roadmap", label: "Roadmap" },
  {
    href: "https://github.com/Public-Intelligence-Revolution",
    label: "GitHub",
    external: true,
  },
];

export function SiteFooter() {
  return (
    <footer className="space-y-8 pt-16 border-t border-border/20 text-xs text-muted-foreground/60">
      <div className="flex flex-wrap items-center justify-between gap-6">
        <div className="inline-flex items-center gap-2">
          <Logo className="w-4 h-4 text-muted-foreground/50" />
          <span>Public Intelligence — Open Infrastructure Initiative</span>
        </div>
        <nav aria-label="Footer navigation" className="flex flex-wrap gap-x-6 gap-y-2">
          {links.map((link) => (
            <Link
              key={link.href}
              href={link.href}
              className="hover:text-[#D9F99D] transition-colors duration-150"
              target={link.external ? "_blank" : undefined}
              rel={link.external ? "noreferrer" : undefined}
            >
              {link.label}
            </Link>
          ))}
        </nav>
      </div>
      <div className="flex items-center justify-between text-[10px] border-t border-border/10 pt-6 font-mono opacity-80">
        <p>© {new Date().getFullYear()} Public Intelligence. Released under the MIT License.</p>
        <p>VER_0.1.0 // FOUNDATIONAL_RELEASE</p>
      </div>
    </footer>
  );
}
````

src/components/page-header.tsx
````
import * as React from "react";

type PageHeaderProps = {
  kicker: string;
  title: string;
  description?: string;
};

export function PageHeader({ kicker, title, description }: PageHeaderProps) {
  return (
    <header className="space-y-6">
      <span className="text-xs font-mono uppercase tracking-wider text-[#D9F99D]">
        {kicker}
      </span>
      <div className="space-y-4">
        <h1 className="text-4xl font-semibold tracking-tight text-foreground sm:text-5xl sm:leading-[1.15]">
          {title}
        </h1>
        {description && (
          <p className="max-w-3xl text-xl leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-2xl font-light">
            {description}
          </p>
        )}
      </div>
    </header>
  );
}
````

              Distributed Inference Coordination
            </h2>
            <p className="max-w-2xl text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">
              A conceptual schematic showing how workloads are routed from client interfaces to geographic nodes. The active path highlights the coordinated execution of an inference query.

                <span className="text-xs font-mono text-[#D9F99D]">01</span>
                <h3 className="text-base font-semibold">Community Owned</h3>
              </div>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">

              </div>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">

                <h3 className="text-base font-semibold">Durable Simplicity</h3>
              </div>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">

              </p>
            </div>

          <div className="flex items-center gap-3">
            <span className="h-1.5 w-1.5 rounded-full bg-[#D9F99D]" />

import { PageShell } from "@/components/page-shell";

export default function VisionPage() {
  return (

              <span className="text-xs font-mono uppercase tracking-wider text-[#D9F99D]">01 // MISSION</span>

            </div>

              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                Public Intelligence exists to help individuals and organizations
                contribute compute resources to a shared network for hosting,
                serving, and improving frontier open-source AI models.
              </p>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                The project is open source, modular, and designed for long-term sustainability, functioning as public infrastructure for AI.
              </p>
            </div>
          </div>
        </section>

        {/* WHY IT EXISTS */}
        <section aria-labelledby="why-heading" className="space-y-6 pt-6 border-t border-border/40">

              <span className="text-xs font-mono uppercase tracking-wider text-[#D9F99D]">02 // RATIONALE</span>
              <h2 id="why-heading" className="text-lg font-semibold text-foreground mt-2">
                Why It Exists
              </h2>
            </div>
            <div className="md:col-span-2 space-y-4">
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                Frontier AI currently depends on large amounts of infrastructure
                controlled by a small number of organizations. Open-source models
                are becoming more capable, but serving them at scale remains
                expensive and operationally complex.
              </p>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                Public Intelligence is researching and building a distributed alternative that lowers the barrier to hosting powerful systems, keeping computational access open and decentralized.
              </p>
            </div>
          </div>

                Long-Term Direction
              </h2>
            </div>
            <div className="md:col-span-2 space-y-4">
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                The long-term goal is public infrastructure for AI: a network of
                independently operated systems that can collectively function as one
                global AI platform.
              </p>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground sm:text-base">
                No single repository represents the full project. The Website, Scheduler,
                Node runtime, communication protocols, SDKs, monitoring, and developer
                tools are expected to evolve as focused, replaceable components of a larger ecosystem.
              </p>
            </div>
          </div>
        </section>

        {/* ENGINEERING VALUES */}
        <section aria-labelledby="values-heading" className="space-y-8 pt-6 border-t border-border/40">

            <span className="text-xs font-mono uppercase tracking-wider text-[#D9F99D]">04 // METHODOLOGY</span>
            <h2 id="values-heading" className="text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight text-foreground">
              Engineering Philosophy
            </h2>
            <p className="max-w-2xl text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">
              We prioritize durable, long-term decisions over rapid short-term development. Our values guide every design choices.
            </p>
          </div>

          <div className="grid gap-x-12 gap-y-10 md:grid-cols-2 pt-4">
            <div className="space-y-3">
              <div className="flex items-center gap-3 text-foreground">
                <svg className="w-5 h-5 text-[#D9F99D]" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5">
                  <path d="M12 8V12L15 15" stroke="currentColor" />
                  <circle cx="12" cy="12" r="9" stroke="currentColor" strokeOpacity="0.3" />

                </svg>
                <h3 className="text-base font-semibold">Documentation First</h3>
              </div>
              <p className="text-sm leading-relaxed text-muted-foreground">
                Specs and reasoning are drafted and peer-reviewed before any implementation work, serving as a unified system spec.
              </p>
            </div>

            <div className="space-y-3">
              <div className="flex items-center gap-3 text-foreground">
                <svg className="w-5 h-5 text-[#D9F99D]" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5">
                  <circle cx="12" cy="12" r="9" stroke="currentColor" strokeOpacity="0.3" />
                  <path d="M12 7v10" stroke="currentColor" />
                  <path d="M7 12h10" stroke="currentColor" />

# Project Analysis: Public Intelligence Website

## 1. Project Summary

**Public Intelligence** is an open engineering initiative building globally distributed AI infrastructure. The website serves as the public face of this initiative, documenting its vision, architecture, roadmap, and providing pathways for contribution. Built with Next.js (App Router), TypeScript, and Tailwind CSS, the site follows a documentation-first approach with a clean, technical aesthetic targeting developers, researchers, and potential contributors.

The site consists of six main pages:
- **Home** - Introduction with hero section
- **Vision** - Mission and strategic intent
- **Architecture** - Technical system design and diagrams
- **Roadmap** - Development timeline and milestones
- **Research** - Technical research and findings
- **Contribute** - Onboarding for new contributors

## 2. Architecture

**Tech Stack:**
- **Framework:** Next.js 14+ (App Router)
- **Language:** TypeScript
- **Styling:** Tailwind CSS with custom design system
- **Component Model:** React Server Components with client-side interactivity where needed
- **Diagrams:** Inline SVG components for technical illustrations

**Project Structure:**
```
src/
├── app/                    # Next.js App Router pages
│   ├── page.tsx           # Home
│   ├── architecture/      # System architecture
│   ├── contribute/        # Contribution guide
│   ├── research/          # Technical research
│   ├── roadmap/           # Development timeline
│   └── vision/            # Mission & intent
├── components/            # Shared UI components
│   ├── architecture-diagram.tsx
│   ├── architecture-diagrams.tsx
│   ├── logo.tsx
│   ├── page-header.tsx
│   ├── page-shell.tsx
│   ├── site-footer.tsx
│   ├── site-header.tsx
│   └── system-diagram.tsx
├── lib/
│   └── utils.ts           # cn() utility for class merging
└── globals.css            # Global styles & Tailwind imports
```

**Key Architectural Patterns:**
- **PageShell** provides consistent layout wrapper with footer
- **PageHeader** standardizes page introductions (kicker, title, description)
- **SVG Diagram Components** encapsulate complex technical illustrations
- **Utility-first CSS** with `cn()` helper for conditional classes

## 3. Design Language

Based on the documentation files (BRAND_GUIDELINES.md, STYLE_GUIDE.md) and component patterns:

**Visual Identity:**
- **Logo:** Orbital/coordinate system motif (SVG with animated orbits)
- **Typography:** System font stack with mono for technical content
- **Color Scheme:** Likely neutral/technical palette (foreground/background variables)
- **Spacing:** Generous vertical rhythm (space-y-24, space-y-20)

**Component Patterns:**
- **PageHeader:** Consistent hierarchy (kicker → title → description)
- **Diagrams:** Monospace, technical aesthetic with SVG precision
- **Layout:** Max-width containers (max-w-4xl, max-w-6xl) with responsive padding
- **Interactive Elements:** Subtle opacity transitions (text-foreground/80)

**Documentation-Driven Design:**
- Content-first approach with clear information hierarchy
- Technical diagrams as first-class citizens
- Minimal decoration, maximum clarity

## 4. Strengths

1. **Clear Information Architecture** - Well-organized pages matching project needs (vision → architecture → roadmap)
2. **Technical Credibility** - Custom SVG diagrams demonstrate depth and precision
3. **Consistent Component System** - PageShell, PageHeader, Logo create cohesive experience
4. **Performance-Oriented** - Next.js App Router with RSC, minimal client-side JS
5. **Contributor-Friendly** - Dedicated contribute page lowers barrier to entry
6. **Documentation Foundation** - Explicit design/development docs ensure consistency
7. **Scalable Structure** - Component separation allows diagram reuse and evolution

## 5. Weaknesses

1. **No Navigation/Wayfinding** - Missing site header with navigation between pages
2. **Home Page Lacks Direction** - Hero doesn't clearly guide users to key sections
3. **Research Page Undefined** - File exists but no summary suggests incomplete content
4. **No Search/Discovery** - No way to find content across pages
5. **Static Diagrams Only** - SVGs lack interactivity (zoom, pan, tooltips)

## Layout Composition Analysis

### 1. Root Layout (`src/app/layout.tsx`)
```tsx
export default function RootLayout({ children }) {
  return (
    <html className={`${geist.variable} dark h-full antialiased`}>
      <body className="min-h-full">
        <SiteHeader />           // ← Rendered ONCE at root level
        {children}               // ← Page content (wrapped in PageShell)
      </body>
    </html>
  );
}
```

### 2. Page Shell (`src/components/page-shell.tsx`)
```tsx
export function PageShell({ children }) {
  return (
    <main className="mx-auto w-full max-w-6xl px-6 py-20 sm:px-8 sm:py-24">
      {children}
      <SiteFooter />             // ← Rendered ONCE per page
    </main>
  );
}
```

### 3. Page Usage (e.g., `src/app/vision/page.tsx`)
```tsx
export default function VisionPage() {
  return (
    <PageShell>                 // ← Wraps page content
      <article>...</article>
    </PageShell>
  );
}
```

## Current Rendering Flow

```
RootLayout
├── SiteHeader (global, single instance)
└── Page Content (e.g., VisionPage)
    └── PageShell
        ├── Article Content
        └── SiteFooter (per-page instance)
```

```
RootLayout
├── SiteHeader (from root layout)
└── Page Content
    └── PageShell
        ├── SiteHeader (DUPLICATE - from my change)
        ├── Article Content
        └── SiteFooter
```

**No duplication exists in the original code.** The architecture is:
- **SiteHeader**: Single global instance in `RootLayout` ✓

- **PageShell**: Content wrapper with footer, used by all pages ✓

# SVG Diagram Consistency Analysis

## Components Analyzed

1. **`system-diagram.tsx`** - Home page hero diagram
2. **`architecture-diagram.tsx`** - Simple 3-node diagram (green theme)
3. **`architecture-diagrams.tsx`** - 5 detailed technical diagrams

---

## Inconsistencies Identified

### 1. **Visual Style & Theme**

| Diagram | Background | Node Style | Stroke | Grid |
|---------|-----------|------------|--------|------|
| `system-diagram` | Grid pattern + rect fill | Dark rect + mono text | `currentColor` (0.15-0.18 opacity) | 20×20, 0.03 opacity |
| `architecture-diagram` | None (transparent) | White rect + green stroke | `#10b981` (2px) | None |
| `architecture-diagrams/*` | Grid pattern + rect fill | Dark rect + mono text | `currentColor` (0.18 opacity) | 20×20, 0.03 opacity |

**Issue:** Two completely different visual languages coexist.

---

### 2. **Typography**

| Diagram | Font Family | Font Size | Font Weight | Color |
|---------|-------------|-----------|-------------|-------|
| `system-diagram` | `font-mono` (inherited) | 10-11px | 500-600 | `#f3f4f6`, `#d1d5db` |
| `architecture-diagram` | Default (sans) | `text-sm` | `font-medium` | `fill-foreground` |
| `architecture-diagrams/*` | `font-mono` (inherited) | 9.5-11px | 400-600 | `#f3f4f6`, `#d1d5db`, `#9ca3af`, `#D9F99D` |

**Issues:**
- `architecture-diagram` uses sans-serif, others use mono
- Inconsistent sizing (9.5px vs 10px vs 11px)
- `architecture-diagram` uses CSS classes, others use inline attributes

---

### 3. **Node Dimensions & Spacing**

| Diagram | Node Width | Node Height | Border Radius | Horizontal Spacing |
|---------|-----------|-------------|---------------|-------------------|
| `system-diagram` | 140 | 60 | 3 | ~230px between centers |
| `architecture-diagram` | 120 | 80 | 8 | ~190px between centers |
| `architecture-diagrams/*` | 140 | 50-60 | 3 | ~230px between centers |

**Issues:**
- `architecture-diagram` uses larger, rounder nodes (120×80, rx=8)
- Others use compact nodes (140×50-60, rx=3)
- Inconsistent vertical positioning

---

### 4. **Stroke Widths**

| Element | `system-diagram` | `architecture-diagram` | `architecture-diagrams/*` |
|---------|------------------|------------------------|---------------------------|
| Node border | 1px | 2px | 1px |
| Connection lines | 1-1.2px | 2px | 1-1.2px |
| Grid lines | 0.5px | N/A | 0.5px |
| Corner ticks | 1px | N/A | 1px |

**Issue:** `architecture-diagram` uses 2px strokes (bolder), others use 1px (technical precision).

---

### 5. **Color Usage**

| Purpose | `system-diagram` | `architecture-diagram` | `architecture-diagrams/*` |
|---------|------------------|------------------------|---------------------------|
| Active/Primary | `#D9F99D` (lime) | `#10b981` (emerald) | `#D9F99D` (lime) |
| Inactive/Secondary | `currentColor` (0.15-0.18) | `#10b981` | `currentColor` (0.1-0.18) |
| Text primary | `#f3f4f6` | `fill-foreground` | `#f3f4f6` |
| Text secondary | `#d1d5db` | N/A | `#d1d5db`, `#9ca3af` |
| Grid | `currentColor` (0.03) | None | `currentColor` (0.03) |

**Issues:**
- Two different "brand greens": `#D9F99D` (lime) vs `#10b981` (emerald)
- `architecture-diagram` uses only emerald, no lime accent
- Inconsistent opacity values for inactive states

---

### 6. **Responsiveness**

| Diagram | ViewBox | Container | Scaling |
|---------|---------|-----------|---------|
| `system-diagram` | 760×180 | `w-full max-w-4xl` | ✓ Scales |
| `architecture-diagram` | 600×300 | `w-full max-w-4xl` | ✓ Scales |
| `architecture-diagrams/*` | 760×220-280 | `w-full max-w-4xl` | ✓ Scales |

**Good:** All use `viewBox` + `w-full max-w-4xl` for responsive scaling.

---

### 7. **Accessibility**

| Diagram | `<title>` | `<desc>` | ARIA | Text Alternative |
|---------|-----------|----------|------|------------------|
| `system-diagram` | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ |
| `architecture-diagram` | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ |
| `architecture-diagrams/*` | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ | ❌ |

**Critical Issue:** **Zero accessibility** - no titles, descriptions, or ARIA labels. Screen readers see empty SVGs.

---

### 8. **Architectural Inconsistencies**

| Aspect | `system-diagram` | `architecture-diagram` | `architecture-diagrams/*` |
|--------|------------------|------------------------|---------------------------|
| Coordinate system | Absolute transforms | Absolute coordinates | Absolute transforms |
| Reusable patterns | ❌ | ❌ | `tickStyles` helper (partial) |
| Arrow markers | ❌ (lines only) | ✓ `markerEnd` | ❌ (lines only) |
| Animation/Interaction | ❌ | `hover:stroke-green-500` | ❌ |

---

## Unified Diagram Language Design

### Design Tokens

```typescript
// Diagram Design System
const DIAGRAM = {
  // Canvas
  canvas: {
    width: 760,
    height: { compact: 180, standard: 240, tall: 280 },
    borderRadius: 6,
    gridSize: 20,
    gridOpacity: 0.03,
  },
  
  // Nodes
  node: {
    width: 140,
    height: { compact: 50, standard: 60 },
    borderRadius: 3,
    strokeWidth: 1,
    strokeOpacity: { inactive: 0.18, active: 0.4 },
    fill: "var(--background, #0f0f11)",
  },
  
  // Typography
  typography: {
    fontFamily: "monospace",
    label: { size: 11, weight: 600, fill: "#f3f4f6" },
    detail: { size: 9.5, weight: 400, fill: "#9ca3af" },
    detailActive: { size: 9.5, weight: 500, fill: "#d1d5db" },
    caption: { size: 9.5, weight: 400, fill: "#9ca3af" },
  },
  
  // Connections
  connection: {
    strokeWidth: { inactive: 1, active: 1.2 },
    strokeOpacity: { inactive: 0.1, active: 1 },
    dashInactive: "3 3",
    markerRadius: 2.5,
  },
  
  // Colors
  color: {
    primary: "#D9F99D",      // Lime - active/accent
    primaryDim: "#D9F99D",   // Same for markers
    textPrimary: "#f3f4f6",
    textSecondary: "#d1d5db",
    textMuted: "#9ca3af",
    borderInactive: "currentColor",
    grid: "currentColor",
  },
  
  // Spacing
  spacing: {
    nodeHorizontalGap: 230,  // Center-to-center
    nodeVerticalGap: 75,     // For stacked nodes
    connectionY: "center",   // Align to node vertical center
  },
  
  // Accessibility
  a11y: {
    titleId: "diagram-title",
    descId: "diagram-desc",
  }
};
```

```
DiagramCanvas (wrapper)
├── GridBackground
├── CornerTicks
├── Node (reusable)
│   ├── NodeRect
│   ├── NodeLabel
│   └── NodeDetail
├── Connection (reusable)
│   ├── ConnectionLine
│   └── ConnectionMarker
└── Caption
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramCanvas.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramCanvasProps = {
  children: React.ReactNode;
  width?: number;
  height?: number;
  className?: string;
  title: string;
  description: string;
};

export function DiagramCanvas({
  children,
  width = 760,
  height = 240,
  className = "",
  title,
  description,
}: DiagramCanvasProps) {
  const titleId = `diagram-title-${React.useId()}`;
  const descId = `diagram-desc-${React.useId()}`;

  return (
    <div className={`w-full flex justify-center py-4 ${className}`}>
      <svg
        viewBox={`0 0 ${width} ${height}`}
        fill="none"
        xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"
        className="w-full max-w-4xl font-mono"
        role="img"
        aria-labelledby={titleId}
        aria-describedby={descId}
      >
        <title id={titleId}>{title}</title>
        <desc id={descId}>{description}</desc>
        <defs>
          <pattern
            id={`grid-${React.useId()}`}
            width="20"
            height="20"
            patternUnits="userSpaceOnUse"
          >
            <path
              d="M 20 0 L 0 0 0 20"
              fill="none"
              stroke="currentColor"
              strokeWidth="0.5"
              strokeOpacity="0.03"
            />
          </pattern>
        </defs>
        <rect
          width={width}
          height={height}
          fill={`url(#grid-${React.useId()})`}
          rx="6"
        />
        {children}
      </svg>
    </div>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramGrid.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramGridProps = {
  width: number;
  height: number;
  patternId: string;
};

export function DiagramGrid({ width, height, patternId }: DiagramGridProps) {
  return (
    <>
      <rect width={width} height={height} fill={`url(#${patternId})`} rx="6" />
      <rect
        x="0.5"
        y="0.5"
        width={width - 1}
        height={height - 1}
        rx="6"
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.08"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d="M 10 0.5 L 0.5 0.5 L 0.5 10"
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M ${width - 10} 0.5 L ${width - 0.5} 0.5 L ${width - 0.5} 10`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M 0.5 ${height - 10} L 0.5 ${height - 0.5} L 10 ${height - 0.5}`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M ${width - 10} ${height - 0.5} L ${width - 0.5} ${height - 0.5} L ${width - 0.5} ${height - 10}`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
    </>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramNode.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramNodeProps = {
  x: number;
  y: number;
  width?: number;
  height?: number;
  label: string;
  detail: string;
  active?: boolean;
  detailActive?: boolean;
  children?: React.ReactNode;
};

const NODE_WIDTH = 140;
const NODE_HEIGHT = 60;
const NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT = 50;
const BORDER_RADIUS = 3;
const STROKE_WIDTH = 1;

export function DiagramNode({
  x,
  y,
  width = NODE_WIDTH,
  height = NODE_HEIGHT,
  label,
  detail,
  active = false,
  detailActive = false,
  children,
}: DiagramNodeProps) {
  return (
    <g transform={`translate(${x}, ${y})`}>
      <rect
        x="0"
        y="0"
        width={width}
        height={height}
        rx={BORDER_RADIUS}
        stroke={active ? "#D9F99D" : "currentColor"}
        strokeWidth={STROKE_WIDTH}
        strokeOpacity={active ? 0.4 : 0.18}
        fill="var(--background, #0f0f11)"
      />
      <text
        x="15"
        y={height === NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT ? 20 : 24}
        fill={active ? "#D9F99D" : "#f3f4f6"}
        fontSize="11"
        fontWeight="600"
      >
        {label}
      </text>
      <text
        x="15"
        y={height === NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT ? 36 : 42}
        fill={detailActive ? "#d1d5db" : active ? "#d1d5db" : "#9ca3af"}
        fontSize="9.5"
        fontWeight={detailActive ? "500" : "400"}
      >
        {detail}
      </text>
      {children}
    </g>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramConnection.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramConnectionProps = {
  x1: number;
  y1: number;
  x2: number;
  y2: number;
  active?: boolean;
  curved?: boolean;
  controlPoint?: { x: number; y: number };
  marker?: boolean;
};

export function DiagramConnection({
  x1,
  y1,
  x2,
  y2,
  active = false,
  curved = false,
  controlPoint,
  marker = false,
}: DiagramConnectionProps) {
  const stroke = active ? "#D9F99D" : "currentColor";
  const strokeWidth = active ? 1.2 : 1;
  const strokeOpacity = active ? 1 : 0.1;
  const strokeDasharray = active ? "none" : "3 3";

  if (curved && controlPoint) {
    return (
      <path
        d={`M ${x1} ${y1} Q ${controlPoint.x} ${controlPoint.y} ${x2} ${y2}`}
        stroke={stroke}
        strokeWidth={strokeWidth}
        strokeOpacity={strokeOpacity}
        strokeDasharray={strokeDasharray}
        fill="none"
        markerEnd={marker ? "url(#arrowhead)" : undefined}
      />
    );
  }

  return (
    <line
      x1={x1}
      y1={y1}
      x2={x2}
      y2={y2}
      stroke={stroke}
      strokeWidth={strokeWidth}
      strokeOpacity={strokeOpacity}
      strokeDasharray={strokeDasharray}
      markerEnd={marker ? "url(#arrowhead)" : undefined}
    />
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramMarker.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramMarkerProps = {
  cx: number;
  cy: number;
  r?: number;
  fill?: string;
};

export function DiagramMarker({ cx, cy, r = 2.5, fill = "#D9F99D" }: DiagramMarkerProps) {
  return <circle cx={cx} cy={cy} r={r} fill={fill} />;
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramCaption.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramCaptionProps = {
  x: number;
  y: number;
  text: string;
  fill?: string;
  fontSize?: number;
  textAnchor?: "start" | "middle" | "end";
};

export function DiagramCaption({
  x,
  y,
  text,
  fill = "#9ca3af",
  fontSize = 9.5,
  textAnchor = "middle",
}: DiagramCaptionProps) {
  return (
    <text
      x={x}
      y={y}
      fill={fill}
      fontSize={fontSize}
      fontWeight="400"
      textAnchor={textAnchor}
    >
      {text}
    </text>
  );
}

src/components/diagram/ArrowheadDef.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

export function ArrowheadDef() {
  return (
    <defs>
      <marker
        id="arrowhead"
        markerWidth="10"
        markerHeight="7"
        refX="0"
        refY="3.5"
        orient="auto"
      >
        <polygon points="0 0, 10 3.5, 0 7" fill="#D9F99D" />
      </marker>
    </defs>
  );
}

import * as React from "react";
import {
  DiagramCanvas,
  DiagramGrid,
  DiagramNode,
  DiagramConnection,
  DiagramMarker,
  DiagramCaption,
  ArrowheadDef,
} from "@/components/diagram";

// 1. Overall System Topology
export function OverallSystemDiagram() {
  const width = 760;
  const height = 220;
  const patternId = "grid-system-overall";
  const nodeY = 80;
  const connectionY = 110;
  const nodeWidth = 140;
  const nodeHeight = 60;
  const nodeSpacing = 230;
  const startX = 80;

  return (
    <DiagramCanvas
      width={width}
      height={height}
      title="Overall System Topology"
      description="Three-node system architecture: Website Portal entry point, Scheduler Core control plane, and Node Network execution plane. Connections show data flow from website to scheduler to compute nodes."
    >
      <DiagramGrid width={width} height={height} patternId={patternId} />
      <ArrowheadDef />

      {/* Node 1: Website */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[WEBSITE_PORTAL]"
        detail="Entry & Onboard"
      />

      {/* Node 2: Scheduler */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX + nodeSpacing}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[SCHEDULER_CORE]"
        detail="Control Plane"
      >
        <DiagramMarker cx={125} cy={15} />
      </DiagramNode>

      {/* Node 3: Contributed Nodes */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX + nodeSpacing * 2}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[NODE_NETWORK]"
        detail="Execution Plane"
      />

      {/* Connections */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={startX + nodeWidth}
        y1={connectionY}
        x2={startX + nodeSpacing}
        y2={connectionY}
      />
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={startX + nodeSpacing + nodeWidth}
        y1={connectionY}
        x2={startX + nodeSpacing * 2}
        y2={connectionY}
        active
      />

      <DiagramMarker cx={startX + nodeSpacing + nodeWidth - 45} cy={connectionY} />
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

// 2. Request Flow
export function RequestFlowDiagram() {
  const width = 760;
  const height = 240;
  const patternId = "grid-flow-request";
  const nodeY = 90;
  const connectionY = 120;
  const nodeWidth = 140;
  const nodeSpacing = 230;
  const startX = 80;

  return (
    <DiagramCanvas
      width={width}
      height={height}
      title="Request Flow"
      description="Request lifecycle from client submission through scheduler routing to node execution. Active path highlighted showing successful routing to EU-West node with direct result return path."
    >
      <DiagramGrid width={width} height={height} patternId={patternId} />
      <ArrowheadDef />

      {/* Node 1: Client */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[CLIENT_INTERFACE]"
        detail="Status: SUBMITTING"
      />

      {/* Node 2: Scheduler */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX + nodeSpacing}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[SCHEDULER_CORE]"
        detail="Status: ROUTING"
      />

      {/* Node 3: Selected Compute Node */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={startX + nodeSpacing * 2}
        y={nodeY}
        label="[NODE_EU_WEST]"
        detail="Status: EXECUTING"
        active
        detailActive
      />

      {/* Active Connection Paths */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={startX + nodeWidth}
        y1={connectionY}
        x2={startX + nodeSpacing}
        y2={connectionY}
        active
      />
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={startX + nodeSpacing + nodeWidth}
        y1={connectionY}
        x2={startX + nodeSpacing * 2}
        y2={connectionY}
        active
      />

      {/* Signal indicators on the active loop */}
      <DiagramMarker cx={startX + nodeWidth + 45} cy={connectionY} />
      <DiagramMarker cx={startX + nodeSpacing * 2 - 45} cy={connectionY} />

      {/* Direct Output Return Path (Subtle feedback loop at bottom) */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={startX + nodeSpacing * 2 + nodeWidth - 30}
        y1={connectionY + 30}
        x2={startX + 30}
        y2={connectionY + 30}
        curved
        controlPoint={{ x: width / 2, y: connectionY + 70 }}
      />
      <DiagramCaption
        x={width / 2}
        y={connectionY + 65}
        text="DIRECT_RESULT_PAYLOAD (verification_loop)"
      />
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

// 3. Geographic Scheduling
export function GeographicSchedulingDiagram() {
  const width = 760;
  const height = 280;
  const patternId = "grid-geo-scheduling";
  const schedulerX = 80;
  const schedulerY = 110;
  const nodeX = 480;
  const nodeWidth = 140;
  const nodeHeight = 50;
  const nodeSpacing = 75;
  const startY = 40;

  return (
    <DiagramCanvas
      width={width}
      height={height}
      title="Geographic Scheduling"
      description="Scheduler routing decision showing three candidate nodes with latency measurements. EU-West selected as minimum latency (12ms) vs US-East (78ms) and AP-South (284ms)."
    >
      <DiagramGrid width={width} height={height} patternId={patternId} />
      <ArrowheadDef />

      {/* Scheduler Node (Left Column) */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={schedulerX}
        y={schedulerY}
        label="[SCHEDULER_CORE]"
        detail="Latency Engine"
      />

      {/* Nodes (Right Column Stacked) */}
      {/* Node 1: US-East */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={nodeX}
        y={startY}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_US_EAST]"
        detail="Latency: 78ms"
      />

      {/* Node 2: EU-West (Selected) */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={nodeX}
        y={startY + nodeSpacing}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_EU_WEST]"
        detail="Latency: 12ms (MIN)"
        active
        detailActive
      />

      {/* Node 3: AP-South */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={nodeX}
        y={startY + nodeSpacing * 2}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_AP_SOUTH]"
        detail="Latency: 284ms"
      />

      {/* Routing branches */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={schedulerX + nodeWidth}
        y1={schedulerY + 30}
        x2={nodeX}
        y2={startY + nodeHeight / 2}
        curved
        controlPoint={{ x: 350, y: 65 }}
      />
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={schedulerX + nodeWidth}
        y1={schedulerY + 30}
        x2={nodeX}
        y2={startY + nodeSpacing + nodeHeight / 2}
        active
      />
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={schedulerX + nodeWidth}
        y1={schedulerY + 30}
        x2={nodeX}
        y2={startY + nodeSpacing * 2 + nodeHeight / 2}
        curved
        controlPoint={{ x: 350, y: 215 }}
      />

      <DiagramMarker cx={350} cy={schedulerY + 30} />
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

// 4. Distributed Inference
export function DistributedInferenceDiagram() {
  const width = 760;
  const height = 280;
  const patternId = "grid-inf-distributed";
  const schedulerX = 80;
  const schedulerY = 110;
  const nodeWidth = 140;
  const nodeHeight = 50;

  return (
    <DiagramCanvas
      width={width}
      height={height}
      title="Distributed Inference Pipeline"
      description="Model layer partitioning across three compute shards. Scheduler partitions layers 1-12 to Shard A, 13-24 to Shard B, 25-36 to Shard C. Pipeline flow shown with active connections."
    >
      <DiagramGrid width={width} height={height} patternId={patternId} />
      <ArrowheadDef />

      {/* Scheduler (Left) */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={schedulerX}
        y={schedulerY}
        label="[SCHEDULER_CORE]"
        detail="Layer Partitioner"
      />

      {/* Pipeline Shards */}
      {/* Shard A */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={320}
        y={60}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_SHARD_A]"
        detail="Layers: 1 - 12"
        active
        detailActive
      />

      {/* Shard B */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={520}
        y={60}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_SHARD_B]"
        detail="Layers: 13 - 24"
        active
        detailActive
      />

      {/* Shard C */}
      <DiagramNode
        x={420}
        y={170}
        width={nodeWidth}
        height={nodeHeight}
        label="[NODE_SHARD_C]"
        detail="Layers: 25 - 36"
        active
        detailActive
      />

      {/* Pipeline connection paths */}
      {/* Scheduler -> Shard A */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={schedulerX + nodeWidth}
        y1={schedulerY + 30}
        x2={320}
        y2={85}
        active
      />

      {/* Shard A -> Shard B */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={460}
        y1={85}
        x2={520}
        y2={85}
        active
      />

      {/* Shard B -> Shard C */}
      <DiagramConnection
        x1={590}
        y1={110}
        x2={490}
        y2={170}
        active
      />

      {/* Flow ticks along the pipeline */}
      <DiagramMarker cx={270} cy={112.5} />
      <DiagramMarker cx={490} cy={85} />
      <DiagramMarker cx={540} cy={140} />
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

// 5. Future Architecture
export function PlatformStackDiagram() {
  const width = 760;
  const height = 240;
  const patternId = "grid-stack-platform";
  const layerX = 120;
  const layerWidth = 520;
  const layerHeight = 35;
  const layerSpacing = 45;
  const startY = 30;

  const layers = [
    {
      label: "APPLICATION / API LAYER",
      detail: "Client SDKs, telemetry portals, developer API endpoints",
      y: startY,
      active: false,
    },
    {
      label: "ORCHESTRATION & COORDINATION LAYER",
      detail: "Geographic scheduling engine, node registries, queue models",
      y: startY + layerSpacing,
      active: true,
    },
    {
      label: "DECENTRALIZED TRANSPORT LAYER",
      detail: "P2P overlay routing, message heartbeats, secure gRPC tunnels",
      y: startY + layerSpacing * 2,
      active: false,
    },
    {
      label: "LOCAL HARDWARE EXECUTION RUNTIME",
      detail: "CUDA/ROCm device engines, local resource benchmarks, sandboxes",
      y: startY + layerSpacing * 3,
      active: false,
    },
  ];

  return (
    <DiagramCanvas
      width={width}
      height={height}
      title="Future Platform Stack Architecture"
      description="Four-layer platform stack: Application API layer, Orchestration & Coordination layer (active), Decentralized Transport layer, and Local Hardware Execution Runtime layer. Each layer spans full width with descriptive details."
    >
      <DiagramGrid width={width} height={height} patternId={patternId} />
      <ArrowheadDef />

      {layers.map((layer, index) => (
        <DiagramNode
          key={index}
          x={layerX}
          y={layer.y}
          width={layerWidth}
          height={layerHeight}
          label={layer.label}
          detail={layer.detail}
          active={layer.active}
          detailActive={layer.active}
        />
      ))}
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

import * as React from "react";
import {

export function SystemDiagram() {

  const height = 180;
  const patternId = "grid-home-system";

  const connectionY = 90;
  const nodeWidth = 140;
  const nodeHeight = 60;

  return (

        active
      />

      {/* Data indicator dot */}
      <DiagramMarker cx={startX + nodeSpacing * 2 - 45} cy={connectionY} />
    </DiagramCanvas>
  );
}

src/components/diagram/DiagramCanvas.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramCanvasProps = {
  children: React.ReactNode;
  width?: number;
  height?: number;
  className?: string;
  title: string;
  description: string;
};

export function DiagramCanvas({
  children,
  width = 760,
  height = 240,
  className = "",
  title,
  description,
}: DiagramCanvasProps) {
  const titleId = `diagram-title-${React.useId()}`;
  const descId = `diagram-desc-${React.useId()}`;

  return (
    <div className={`w-full flex justify-center py-4 ${className}`}>
      <svg
        viewBox={`0 0 ${width} ${height}`}
        fill="none"
        xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"
        className="w-full max-w-4xl font-mono"
        role="img"
        aria-labelledby={titleId}
        aria-describedby={descId}
      >
        <title id={titleId}>{title}</title>
        <desc id={descId}>{description}</desc>
        <defs>
          <pattern
            id={`grid-${React.useId()}`}
            width="20"
            height="20"
            patternUnits="userSpaceOnUse"
          >
            <path
              d="M 20 0 L 0 0 0 20"
              fill="none"
              stroke="currentColor"
              strokeWidth="0.5"
              strokeOpacity="0.03"
            />
          </pattern>
        </defs>
        <rect
          width={width}
          height={height}
          fill={`url(#grid-${React.useId()})`}
          rx="6"
        />
        {children}
      </svg>
    </div>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramGrid.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramGridProps = {
  width: number;
  height: number;
  patternId: string;
};

export function DiagramGrid({ width, height, patternId }: DiagramGridProps) {
  return (
    <>
      <rect width={width} height={height} fill={`url(#${patternId})`} rx="6" />
      <rect
        x="0.5"
        y="0.5"
        width={width - 1}
        height={height - 1}
        rx="6"
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.08"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d="M 10 0.5 L 0.5 0.5 L 0.5 10"
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M ${width - 10} 0.5 L ${width - 0.5} 0.5 L ${width - 0.5} 10`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M 0.5 ${height - 10} L 0.5 ${height - 0.5} L 10 ${height - 0.5}`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
      <path
        d={`M ${width - 10} ${height - 0.5} L ${width - 0.5} ${height - 0.5} L ${width - 0.5} ${height - 10}`}
        stroke="currentColor"
        strokeWidth="1"
        strokeOpacity="0.25"
        fill="none"
      />
    </>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramNode.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramNodeProps = {
  x: number;
  y: number;
  width?: number;
  height?: number;
  label: string;
  detail: string;
  active?: boolean;
  detailActive?: boolean;
  children?: React.ReactNode;
};

const NODE_WIDTH = 140;
const NODE_HEIGHT = 60;
const NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT = 50;
const BORDER_RADIUS = 3;
const STROKE_WIDTH = 1;

export function DiagramNode({
  x,
  y,
  width = NODE_WIDTH,
  height = NODE_HEIGHT,
  label,
  detail,
  active = false,
  detailActive = false,
  children,
}: DiagramNodeProps) {
  return (
    <g transform={`translate(${x}, ${y})`}>
      <rect
        x="0"
        y="0"
        width={width}
        height={height}
        rx={BORDER_RADIUS}
        stroke={active ? "#D9F99D" : "currentColor"}
        strokeWidth={STROKE_WIDTH}
        strokeOpacity={active ? 0.4 : 0.18}
        fill="var(--background, #0f0f11)"
      />
      <text
        x="15"
        y={height === NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT ? 20 : 24}
        fill={active ? "#D9F99D" : "#f3f4f6"}
        fontSize="11"
        fontWeight="600"
      >
        {label}
      </text>
      <text
        x="15"
        y={height === NODE_HEIGHT_COMPACT ? 36 : 42}
        fill={detailActive ? "#d1d5db" : active ? "#d1d5db" : "#9ca3af"}
        fontSize="9.5"
        fontWeight={detailActive ? "500" : "400"}
      >
        {detail}
      </text>
      {children}
    </g>
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramConnection.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramConnectionProps = {
  x1: number;
  y1: number;
  x2: number;
  y2: number;
  active?: boolean;
  curved?: boolean;
  controlPoint?: { x: number; y: number };
  marker?: boolean;
};

export function DiagramConnection({
  x1,
  y1,
  x2,
  y2,
  active = false,
  curved = false,
  controlPoint,
  marker = false,
}: DiagramConnectionProps) {
  const stroke = active ? "#D9F99D" : "currentColor";
  const strokeWidth = active ? 1.2 : 1;
  const strokeOpacity = active ? 1 : 0.1;
  const strokeDasharray = active ? "none" : "3 3";

  if (curved && controlPoint) {
    return (
      <path
        d={`M ${x1} ${y1} Q ${controlPoint.x} ${controlPoint.y} ${x2} ${y2}`}
        stroke={stroke}
        strokeWidth={strokeWidth}
        strokeOpacity={strokeOpacity}
        strokeDasharray={strokeDasharray}
        fill="none"
        markerEnd={marker ? "url(#arrowhead)" : undefined}
      />
    );
  }

  return (
    <line
      x1={x1}
      y1={y1}
      x2={x2}
      y2={y2}
      stroke={stroke}
      strokeWidth={strokeWidth}
      strokeOpacity={strokeOpacity}
      strokeDasharray={strokeDasharray}
      markerEnd={marker ? "url(#arrowhead)" : undefined}
    />
  );
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramMarker.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramMarkerProps = {
  cx: number;
  cy: number;
  r?: number;
  fill?: string;
};

export function DiagramMarker({ cx, cy, r = 2.5, fill = "#D9F99D" }: DiagramMarkerProps) {
  return <circle cx={cx} cy={cy} r={r} fill={fill} />;
}
```

src/components/diagram/DiagramCaption.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

type DiagramCaptionProps = {
  x: number;
  y: number;
  text: string;
  fill?: string;
  fontSize?: number;
  textAnchor?: "start" | "middle" | "end";
};

export function DiagramCaption({
  x,
  y,
  text,
  fill = "#9ca3af",
  fontSize = 9.5,
  textAnchor = "middle",
}: DiagramCaptionProps) {
  return (
    <text
      x={x}
      y={y}
      fill={fill}
      fontSize={fontSize}
      fontWeight="400"
      textAnchor={textAnchor}
    >
      {text}
    </text>
  );
}

src/components/diagram/ArrowheadDef.tsx
```
import * as React from "react";

export function ArrowheadDef() {
  return (
    <defs>
      <marker
        id="arrowhead"
        markerWidth="10"
        markerHeight="7"
        refX="0"
        refY="3.5"
        orient="auto"
      >
        <polygon points="0 0, 10 3.5, 0 7" fill="#D9F99D" />
      </marker>
    </defs>
  );
}
